=== [[Talk:The Apprentice (UK TV series)#rfc_1C16235|Talk:The Apprentice (UK TV series)]] expired 2016-12-18 00:01 ===
* Id: 1C16235
* User: GUtt01
* Date: 2016-11-17 23:03:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|750129457|MEDIA 750129457}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|755430984|MEDIA 755430984}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I would like to put forward an important discussion in regards to the information that has been put out in the articles that cover each series of ''The Apprentice (UK)''. This discussion is an important one that needs to be looked into, as I, an editor for this site, have begun to question whether the information in these articles is encyclopedic, or whether the articles are beginning to become treated as a Blog, which Wikipedia is not designed as.  As an editor who has worked on these pages, I have been a part of adding in information to discuss the respective episodes, but have begun to question whether the information being put in by myself, and other editors, regardless of whether it is later changed, added to, or deleted, is now really relevant, and more importantly sticks to Wikipedia's principle of providing encyclopedic information.

The chief problem on these articles is in regards to information on episodes.  The layout for this information is that it states the Air Date for each episode in each series, the teams and their candidates within, the task being undertaken on that episode and a review of what happened, results of the task and who won and what they were rewarded with, who was brought back to the final boardroom, who was fired or left, the panellist for the sister show that came after that episode, and notes in regards to events in the episode (i.e. a candidate who made a mistake and tried to lie about it).

Other information in this article, from the lead, the candidate and weekly results, criticism and controversy, and ratings, appears to be fine, with some area certainly backed by citations to prove it.  What I want to know is this - Should the information within the Episode section of each article for these series, be changed or stick to the way it is presented? Does it constitute as being a Blog and thus go against [[Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not]] in regards to this?  And if the first two questions generate "Yes" as an answer, would changing it to listing the episodes in a table, keeping the Air Date and the episode's title, and writing out a short summary of the episode (as with most TV programmes), be more appropriate?

I await word from others on what they think. [[User:GUtt01|GUtt01]] ([[User talk:GUtt01|talk]]) 23:03, 17 November 2016 (UTC)}}

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|755614904|PROP 755614904}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The proposal is simple, this is one of vital projects on Wiki that holds the responsibility of handling the good content. Since its inception it went on without any leadership, I feel electing coordinators will help better functioning of the project. My proposal is to elect one main coordinator, another 2‚Äì4 assisting coords, and 1-2 coords for each topic area. This will help in effectively handling the nominations, look over the reviews, address the second opinions etc. Please share you views. There is no requirement that the users with highest number of edits will have to be coords. Regards, [[User:Krishna Chaitanya Velaga|Krishna Chaitanya Velaga]] ([[User_talk:Krishna Chaitanya Velaga|talk]]&nbsp;&bull;&#32;[[Special:EmailUser/Krishna_Chaitanya_Velaga|mail]]) 04:18, 11 December 2016 (UTC)}}

== Feedback requested: [[Wikipedia:Good article nominations/Report|Backlog Report]] link preferences '''

For those who don't know, the [[User:StatisticianBot|bot]] that previously updated [[Wikipedia:Good article nominations/Report]] has been down for some time. I'm currently working on a replacement, [[User:WugBot|WugBot]] (see [[Wikipedia:Bots/Requests for approval/WugBot|BRFA]]). [[User:BlueMoonset|BlueMoonset]] and I have been [[User_talk:Wugapodes#WugBot_output|discussing]] where the links on that page should point to. Currently I have it set up so that the links go directly to the review page of the article (if it exists, to the talk page otherwise) which is different from how the predecesor, StatisticianBot, formatted the links. Previously, the links would go to the GAN page and jump to the section where the nomination is. BlueMoonset makes a good case for the previous format, but I think we'd both like to hear wider input on what others would prefer.

'''TL;DR''': Where should the links on [[Wikipedia:Good article nominations/Report]] point, the GAN page as previously, the article's review page as currently, or some other option? === [[Talk:Alice Corp. v. CLS Bank International#rfc_0C36AA9|Talk:Alice Corp. v. CLS Bank International]] expired 2016-12-19 17:01 ===
* Id: 0C36AA9
* User: Jytdog
* Date: 2016-12-06 02:42:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|753257699|BIO 753257699}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|753257703|POL 753257703}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|755693328|BIO 755693328}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|755693332|POL 755693332}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This article currently contains the following image and content:

Image: [[:File:Cartoon of Justice Thomas refusing to explain Alice ruling.jpg]] 

Content:
;''Law Comics'' commentary on "we need not labor..."

''Law Comics'' cartooned Justice Thomas saying that "we need not labor..." and replied "yes you do!" while wagging a finger at him as an accompanying article asserted that his opinion ‚Äúbaulked at the messy, challenging issues surrounding software‚Äù and was ‚Äúnot a particularly useful‚Äù decision about patenting software.<ref>[http://www.wired.co.uk/news/archive/2014-06/30/alice-in-patentland ‚ÄúAlice in Patentland is a comic about patent law‚Äù], {{smallcaps|Wired}}.</ref>
{{reflist-talk}}

The cartoon has been [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alice_Corp._v._CLS_Bank_International&type=revision&diff=753011459&oldid=746028570 objected to], as being racist. Thomas is a living person so [[WP:BLP]] may be at play. 

There is a separate discussion ongoing about deleting the image, [[Wikipedia:Files_for_discussion/2016_August_15#File:Cartoon_of_Justice_Thomas_refusing_to_explain_Alice_ruling.jpg|here]]. 

With regard to this article, should the image and content be retained/kept or be removed?  [[User:Jytdog|Jytdog]] ([[User talk:Jytdog|talk]]) 02:42, 6 December 2016 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Deletion process#rfc_D0344A3|Wikipedia talk:Deletion process]] expired 2016-12-21 02:01 ===
* Id: D0344A3
* User: BU Rob13
* Date: 2016-11-21 01:03:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|751814272|POLICY 751814272}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|755945014|POLICY 755945014}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
No-one's formally proposed this solution above, but it certainly has received a lot of support. Let's see if there's actual consensus for it. I propose changing the text of [[WP:NOQUORUM]] to the following:

{{blockquote|If a nomination has received no comments from any editor besides the nominator and the article hasn't been declined for proposed deletion in the past, the closing administrator should treat the AfD nomination as an expired PROD. Generally, this will result in soft deletion (see below), but administrators should evaluate the nominating statement as they would a PROD rationale. See [[WP:PROD]] for more details.

If the nomination has received very few comments, has received no comments but appears controversial to the closing administrator, or has been declined for proposed deletion in the past, the discussion may be closed at the closer's discretion and best judgement. Common options include, but are not limited to:

* relisting the discussion (see the section '[[#Relisting discussions|Relisting discussions]]');
* closing as "no consensus" with no prejudice against speedy renomination ('''NPASR'''); and
* closing in favour of the nominator's stated proposal.
* '''Soft deletion''' is a special kind of deletion which may be used after an article's deletion discussion. If a deletion discussion sees very little discussion even after being relisted several times, the administrator can close the discussion as soft delete and delete the page. However, in this case, the article can be restored for any reason on request. If your article was soft-deleted, you can request it be restored at [[Wikipedia:Requests for undeletion|Requests for undeletion]].  The closer should make it clear the deletion is a soft delete as part of the close, ideally with a link to this guideline.
* There is consensus among the community that problematic or likely-problematic articles<ref>Usually articles unreferenced for years.</ref> with an appropriate redirection target may be [[WP:BLAR|blanked and redirected]] by any editor if there are no objections. This similarly applies to deletion nominations as well; if no editor suggests that the corresponding article should be kept, then redirection is an option.}}

{{reftalk}}

Note that most of the text is the same, but I have cut out a "special case" where no comments have been made other than the nominator, in which case the nomination will be treated as an expired PROD. In the spirit of our current PROD process, articles that have had a PROD declined will not be considered as expired PRODs, since PRODs are meant to occur only once per article. ~ [[User:BU Rob13|<b>Rob</b><small><sub>13</sub></small>]]<sup style="margin-left:-1.0ex;">[[User talk:BU Rob13|Talk]]</sup> 01:03, 21 November 2016 (UTC)}}

So I am in the process of cleaning up deprecated parameters from templates. This template has a number of them. During a discussion about these parameters (see above) it came to light that some parameters in the template are all one word (for example {{param|foobar}}) while others have an underscore (such as {{param|foo_bar}}. The question on the table is regarding making all the template parameters consistent. I will gladly be responsible for changing the transclusions (it will be done with a bot), updating the template and the template documentation, etc. I just want to make sure that a consensus is reached! For simplicity sake, the question on the table for '''support''' or '''oppose''' is:
:''Should all multi-word parameters in the template (such as {{param|expansiondraftyear}}) be formatted to use underscores (i.e. {{param|expansion_draft_year}}.''
Obviously all comments comments are welcome! Not just support/oppose. Looking forward to hearing all input! Also if there are additional parameters that are deprecated and should be removed, let's be sure to get that well documented so I can hit them all when I run my bot. --[[User:Zackmann08|<span style="color:DarkTurquoise;">Zackmann08</span>]] (<sup>[[User_talk:Zackmann08|Talk to me]]</sup>/<sub>[[Special:Contributions/Zackmann08|<span style="color:orange;">What I been doing</span>]]</sub>) 06:18, 25 November 2016 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:United States presidential elections in which the winner lost the popular vote#rfc_22C665B|Talk:United States presidential elections in which the winner lost the popular vote]] expired 2016-12-26 16:01 ===
* Id: 22C665B
* User: LavaBaron
* Date: 2016-12-03 18:25:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|752850499|POL 752850499}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|756747369|POL 756747369}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
We seem to be using terms like "win" and "lose" fast and loose. Can we take a moment to build a consensus as to what it means to "lose" the popular vote so we have an objective standard to measure future edits and avoid edit-warring? Here are a few options: 
#Lose the Popular Vote means to Secure Less than 50% of the Popular Vote
#Lose the Popular Vote means to Secure Fewer Popular Votes than the Person who Received the Most Popular Votes 
#Lose the Popular Vote means to Secure Fewer Popular Votes than Any Other Candidate 
<small>'''If standard #1''' is adopted, Donald Trump would have lost the popular vote in 2016 (along with every other candidate, but this would not materially change the article since he would still be listed as a president who "won" despite "losing"). '''If standard #2''' is adopted it would mean Donald Trump lost the popular vote in 2016 along with every other candidate ''except'' Hillary Clinton, but - again - the article would not materially change (Trump would still be listed as a president who "won" despite "losing").  '''If standard #3''' is adopted, ''only'' Frank Atwood [http://uselectionatlas.org/RESULTS/national.php?year=2016&minper=0&f=0&off=0&elect=0] would have lost the popular vote in 2016 as he received 337 votes, fewer than any other candidate (this would materially change the article).</small>
[[User:LavaBaron|LavaBaron]] ([[User talk:LavaBaron|talk]]) 18:25, 3 December 2016 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Bipartisan Report#rfc_B923DD9|Talk:Bipartisan Report]] expired 2016-12-26 17:01 ===
* Id: B923DD9
* User: PCHS-NJROTC
* Date: 2016-12-11 01:42:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|754140523|MEDIA 754140523}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|754140526|POL 754140526}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|756753771|MEDIA 756753771}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|756753776|POL 756753776}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This article was recently created by me, and shortly thereafter [[User:Bearcat]] disputed the neutrality of this article. Without discussion, an anonymous editor using [http://www.gogoair.com/ airplane Wi-Fi] proceeded to remove a lot of referenced information which he [[WP:IDONTLIKEIT|must not have liked]]. A neutral tone is important, and making the language a little less harsh is understandable, but removing referenced information is [[whitewashing]] and a general disservice to readers of Wikipedia. The overwhelming majority of sources criticize the website. [http://www.snopes.com/fox-news-benghazi-probe-hoax/ Snopes has debunked articles published by Bipartisan Report]. This website is documented in reliable sources as essentially being something ran out of someone's basement, using far-fetched headlines as [[click bait]], and the operator of the website doesn't even contest that. In my opinion, this article is not even worth keeping with only three sentences. The article, as it stands now, barely demonstrates [[WP:N|notability]], and it's debatable if it demonstrates it at all since this website is proof that anyone with an internet connected device can make a site "claiming" to be the world's largest newspaper, just as any 13 year old girl can claim to be the world's best soccer player on her Facebook page. I do believe, however, that the article met the requirements of inclusion prior to the reduction in content, as there were numerous [[WP:RS|sources]] cited. I propose reinstating the deleted material, but perhaps in a softer fashion. [[User:PCHS-NJROTC|<font color="red" face="Comic Sans MS">PCHS-NJROTC</font>]] <sup>[[User talk:PCHS-NJROTC|<font color="black" face="Comic Sans MS">(Messages)Growing tired of the bullshit day by day.</font>]]</sup> 01:42, 11 December 2016 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_BDA4433|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2016-12-27 10:01 ===
* Id: BDA4433
* User: Unscintillating
* Date: 2016-12-27 02:16:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|756833836|MEDIA 756833836}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|756833839|SOC 756833839}}

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|756875594|MEDIA 756875594}}

{{rfcquote|text=
'''Hypothesis #1''': <blockquote>Wikipedia readers want reliably sourced information, as available, for a broad range of topics; including the entrants to [[Miss America]] and to [[Miss USA]], each of whom have won notable state-level pageants.</blockquote>
'''Hypothesis #2''':<blockquote>WP:Deletion policy is a "widely accepted standard that all editors should normally follow", and as per [[WP:Deletion policy#Alternatives to deletion]] and [[WP:Deletion policy#CONTENT]], merger of non-notable topics to suitable targets is accepted policy.</blockquote><p>'''History''': [[Miss America]] was established in 1921, and [[Miss USA]] established in 1952.&nbsp; In 1979, [http://deadline.com/2015/07/miss-usa-pageant-smallest-audience-on-record-reelz-1201475424/ Miss USA had 38 million viewers.]&nbsp; As per our [[Miss USA]] article, in the early 1980s, the TV coverage regularly topped the Nielsen ratings.&nbsp; The popularity of these two pageants waned between 1990 and 2000, but since 2010 both have recovered some lost television coverage.&nbsp; <p>'''Associated state-level pageants are notable''': All of these entrants are winners of notable state-level pageants, see [[:Category:Miss USA state pageants]] and [[:Category:Miss America state pageants]].&nbsp; <p>'''Entrants may or may not be Wikipedia notable''': Notability is not a key parameter for inclusion of these individuals, as Wikipedia non-notable topics can be covered as mini-bios at a suitable target topic.&nbsp; <p>'''Common elements in a bio''': The typical state pageant winner is less than 24 years of age, and has competed in several beauty pageants before winning the state title.&nbsp; Winning the state title carries with it some scholarship money and a one-year reign, which means public appearances in various events around the state, as well as the national TV event.&nbsp; Occasionally, these winners are recognized by the state legislature.&nbsp; Besides being state celebrities, these winners typically get limited international coverage, including some coverage in foreign languages.<p>'''Wikiproject Beauty Pageants''': I am not a member of [[WP:WikiProject Beauty Pageants]] and the project page is marked <i>semi-active</i>.&nbsp; One of their strongest proponents, [[User:Dravecky]], died in April of this year.&nbsp; [[User:Unscintillating|Unscintillating]] ([[User talk:Unscintillating|talk]]) 02:16, 27 December 2016 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_F7E87C5|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2016-12-27 16:01 ===
* Id: F7E87C5
* User: Unscintillating

=== [[Talk:Abortion-rights movements#rfc_E00BD28|Talk:Abortion-rights movements]] expired 2016-12-27 22:01 ===
* Id: E00BD28
* User: Elizium23
* Date: 2016-11-27 21:17:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|751795433|POL 751795433}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|756955612|POL 756955612}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
:Background: [[Wikipedia:Requests for comment/Abortion advocacy movement coverage]] and [[Wikipedia:Requests for comment/Abortion article titles]] from 2012. Wikipedia has never been quite sure how to refer to the abortion activism movements, and currently the article titles are set from a narrow consensus at [[Abortion-rights movements]] and [[Anti-abortion movements]]. This RFC instead asks the question: how can we refer to the movements in article prose? This question is necessary because the status quo has gradually settled on a certain balance and I contend that that status is entirely out of balance, a clear and present violation of [[WP:NPOV|Wikipedia's core neutrality policy]] and an affront to the supporters of both movements.
*What is the current status quo? Abortion-rights movements are referred to as "[[pro-choice]]" for example [[NARAL Pro-Choice America]] and [[Planned Parenthood]] and [[:Category:Pro-choice organizations in the United States]]. The only place "[[pro-life]]" survives is [[:Category:American pro-life activists]], a holdout from the Great Renaming in which cats were mostly moved to "anti-abortion", which is the current status quo term for the so-called [[anti-abortion movements]]. Editors simply will not allow anyone or anything to be called "pro-life", whether or not the topic in question clearly transcends anti-abortion, or a preponderance of [[WP:RS]] describe the topic as "pro-life", which would seem to violate [[WP:V]] and [[WP:OR]].
:Therefore, the logic would suggest that "pro-choice", a biased non-neutral term used only by supporters to describe themselves, should be eliminated in order to level the playing field. It is the only way to comply with [[WP:NPOV]] if we are to avoid accusations of [[WP:SYSTEMIC]] bias which would be indicated by the way that the pro-abortion position is given the largesse to self-identify while pro-life is not. So the questions before us are:
# '''How will we refer to abortion-rights movements in article prose?''' (a) pro-abortion (b) pro-choice (c) abortion rights
# '''How will we refer to anti-abortion movements in article prose?''' (a) anti-abortion (b) pro-life (c) opposition to abortion rights
:I suggest that the outcome of this RFC should become binding project-wide so that we have a clear and consistent method of referring to these topics that will not be the subject of constant contention and edit-wars without any clear resolution. [[User:Elizium23|Elizium23]] ([[User talk:Elizium23|talk]]) 21:17, 27 November 2016 (UTC)}}

* Id: BBD19F9
* User: KATMAKROFAN
* Date: 2016-12-28 00:39:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|756978044|UNSORTED 756978044}}

* RFC Text:

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_FC5FE9C|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2016-12-31 04:01 ===
* Id: FC5FE9C
* User: Lx 121
* Date: 2016-12-26 15:32:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|756747361|BIO 756747361}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|756747367|HIST 756747367}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|757335796|POLICY 757335796}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|757335798|PROP 757335798}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|757521668|BIO 757521668}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|757521670|HIST 757521670}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|757521673|POLICY 757521673}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|757521676|PROP 757521676}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
'''''nutshell''''':  ''because'' a photograph of the subject of an article is more accurate than a painting or a drawing (& because the lede image is the first thing most readers will see);  (when they are available) photographs should generally be used ''in preference'' to paintings or drawings, as the ''primary (i.e.: lead) illustration'' of the subject, in an article.


::''(background) I am getting extremely tired of having the same fights, with the same people, again, & Again, & AGAIN; mostly on the same few articles, year in & year out.  So let's "have it out" once & for all;  full-on rfc & '''everybody''' is invited.''


'''BE IT RESOLVED'''

That, as per the requirements of WP:Accuracy and WP:NPOV,

When it comes to "real-world", i.e.: ''non-fictional'' subjects; such as history, biographies, etc.

''When'' photographic images ''illustrating the subject of the article'', which are of acceptable (article-space useable) quality exist, & are available to use (re: copyright, etc.),

& are not in (serious) dispute over matters of factual accuracy (such as identify of the subject, date, or alterations to the image),

the use of such ''photographic images'' should be given ''preference'' and ''precedence'' over the use of paintings, drawings, and other suchlike "interpretive" artworks,

as a/the '''primary illustration''' of the subject in articles;

with allowance for obvious exceptions such as maps, plans, diagrams, etc.; as per common sense and the practical requirements of the subject.

''NOTE THAT'':  this ''in no way'' prohibits the ''inclusion in the article'' of creative artworks depicting or relevant to the subject, as best suits the article; "history of", "in art", "official portraits", etc.

Merely that, ''as primary &/or lead image'' on the article, preference should be given to photographic images ''accurately depicting'' the likeness of the subject, WHEN THEY ARE AVAILABLE, over creative/interpretive artworks.

For reasons of '''accuracy''', ''better'' NPOV, & "best practices" as historical documentation of the subject, and wp:style.

Not to mention basic common sense.

[[User:Lx 121|Lx 121]] ([[User talk:Lx 121|talk]]) 15:32, 26 December 2016 (UTC)}}

* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This article is more likely to be written in [[American English]] than British due to the country's history as a possession of the the [[United States]]. It, along with other [[Central American]] countries, such as the [[Dominican Republic]], [[El Salvador]], [[Guatemala]], and [[Panama]] were under American hegemony most of the 20th century. Panama and the Dominican Republic were even briefly occupied. A request to include the template [[Template:American English|American English]] be included in the talk pages of the articles. [[User:Shhhhwwww!!|Shhhhwwww!!]] ([[User talk:Shhhhwwww!!|talk]]) 08:37, 31 December 2016 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Good article nominations#rfc_D6EA601|Wikipedia talk:Good article nominations]] expired 2016-12-31 18:01 ===
* Id: D6EA601
* User: Lourdes
* Date: 2016-12-01 17:04:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|752520774|POLICY 752520774}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|752520777|PROJ 752520777}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|752520782|PROP 752520782}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|757613576|POLICY 757613576}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|757613579|PROJ 757613579}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|757613580|PROP 757613580}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
[[Wikipedia:Stand-alone lists|Stand-alone lists]] are defined as ''"articles composed of one or more embedded lists, or series of items formatted into a list."'' The current [[Wikipedia:Good article criteria#What cannot be a good article?|good article criteria]] mentions that stand-alone lists should be nominated directly as [[WP:FL|featured lists]] rather than as good articles. Currently, there are a few lists that have good article status: for example, [[List of counties in Delaware]], [[List of Ops (B) staff]] and more... As lists are technically defined as articles, and as there may be lists that may perhaps qualify to be ''good articles'' before being improved to featured list standards, editors may be motivated to develop good quality lists if lists (in other words, articles by definition) may be allowed to be nominated for GA status. In this context, I request for the comments of my fellow editors to the following queries:

#''"Should stand-alone lists be allowed to be nominated as [[WP:GA|good articles]]?"''
#''"Should a new criteria of Good List status be introduced instead of qualifying lists as Good Articles?"''
#''"Should we continue status quo, that is, not change anything and let it continue as it is?"''

Thanks. [[User talk:Lourdes|<span style="color:#0000FF;">'''Lourdes'''</span>]] 17:04, 1 December 2016 (UTC)}}
